The national director of the Anti-Defamation League, Abraham Foxman, condemned the cartoon, stating that "Here's the anti-Semitic notion of Jews and their love for money, the canard that Jews 'control' Wall Street, and a cynical perversion of the Western Wall, the holiest site in Judaism," and "Once again Iran takes the prize for promoting antisemitism."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Algemeiner_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Algemeiner-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Jewish_Chronicle_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Jewish_Chronicle-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ADL_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADL-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Japan" title="Antisemitism in Japan">Antisemitism in Japan</a></div>
<p>The Japanese first learned about antisemitism in 1918, during the cooperation of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a> with the <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a> in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. <a href="/wiki/White_Army#Structure" class="mw-redirect" title="White Army">White Army</a> soldiers had been issued copies of <i>The Protocols of the Elders of Zion</i>, and "The <i>Protocols</i> continue to be used as evidence of Jewish conspiracies even though they are widely acknowledged to be a forgery.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> encouraged Japan to adopt antisemitic policies. In the post-war period, <a href="/wiki/Extremism" title="Extremism">extremist groups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ideologues" class="mw-redirect" title="Ideologues">ideologues</a> have promoted <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">Lebanon</span></h4>
<p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a>, a media network affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>, aired a drama series, <i>The Diaspora</i>, which observers allege is based on historical antisemitic allegations. <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> correspondents who have watched the program says it quotes extensively from the <i>Protocols of the Elders of Zion</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Malaysia" title="History of the Jews in Malaysia">History of the Jews in Malaysia</a></div>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> presently has no substantial Jewish population, the country has reportedly become an example of a phenomenon called "antisemitism without Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his treatise on Malay identity, "The Malay Dilemma," which was published in 1970, Malaysian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mahathir_Mohamad" title="Mahathir Mohamad">Mahathir Mohamad</a> wrote: "The Jews are not only hooked-nosed... but understand money instinctively.... Jewish stinginess and financial wizardry gained them the economic control of Europe and provoked antisemitism which waxed and waned throughout Europe through the ages."<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Malay-language <a href="/wiki/Utusan_Malaysia" title="Utusan Malaysia">Utusan Malaysia</a> daily stated in an editorial that Malaysians "cannot allow anyone, especially the Jews, to interfere secretly in this country's business... When the drums are pounded hard in the name of human rights, the pro-Jewish people will have their best opportunity to interfere in any Islamic country," the newspaper said. "We might not realize that the enthusiasm to support actions such as demonstrations will cause us to help foreign groups succeed in their mission of controlling this country." Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Najib_Razak" title="Najib Razak">Najib Razak</a>'s office subsequently issued a statement late Monday saying Utusan's claim did "not reflect the views of the government."<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestine">Palestine</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tomorrow%27s_Pioneers" title="Tomorrow&#39;s Pioneers">Tomorrow's Pioneers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_Palestinian_territories" title="Racism in the Palestinian territories">Racism in the Palestinian territories</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Textbooks_in_the_Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Textbooks in the Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Textbooks in the Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a></div>
<p><span id="Gaza_&amp;_Palestinian_Territories"></span>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A,_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="792" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1987-004-09A,_Amin_al_Husseini_und_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" class="mw-redirect" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">Haj Amin al-Husseini</a> is a central figure of <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_nationalism" title="Palestinian nationalism">Palestinian nationalism</a> in Mandatory Palestine. He took refuge and collaborated with Nazi Germany during World War II. He met <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> in December 1941. Scholarly opinion is divided on the Mufti's antisemitsm, with many scholars viewing him as a staunch antisemite<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> while some deny the appropriateness of the term, or argue that he became antisemitic.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In March 2011, the Israeli government issued a paper claiming that "Anti-Israel and anti-Semitic messages are heard regularly in the government and private media and in the mosques and are taught in school books," to the extent that they are "an integral part of the fabric of life inside the PA."<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> In August 2012, Israeli Strategic Affairs Ministry director-general Yossi Kuperwasser stated that Palestinian incitement to antisemitism is "going on all the time" and that it is "worrying and disturbing." At an institutional level, he said the PA has been promoting three key messages to the Palestinian people that constitute incitement: "that the Palestinians would eventually be the sole sovereign on all the land from the Jordan River to the Mediterranean Sea; that Jews, especially those who live in Israel, were not really human beings but rather 'the scum of mankind'; and that all tools were legitimate in the struggle against Israel and the Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-kuperwasser_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kuperwasser-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> In August 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>' spokesman in Doha said on live television that <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">Jews use blood to make matzos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Pakistan" title="History of the Jews in Pakistan">History of the Jews in Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Pakistan" title="Antisemitism in Pakistan">Antisemitism in Pakistan</a></div>
<p>The U.S. State Department's first Report on Global Anti-Semitism mentioned a strong feeling of antisemitism in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> In Pakistan, a country without Jewish communities, antisemitic sentiment fanned by antisemitic articles in the press is widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Pakistan, Jews are often regarded as miserly.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> After Israel's independence in 1948, violent incidents occurred against Pakistan's small Jewish community of about 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Bene_Israel" title="Bene Israel">Bene Israel</a> Jews. The <a href="/wiki/Magain_Shalome_Synagogue" title="Magain Shalome Synagogue">Magain Shalome Synagogue</a> in Karachi was attacked, as were individual Jews. The persecution of Jews resulted in their exodus via India to Israel (see <a href="/wiki/Pakistanis_in_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistanis in Israel">Pakistanis in Israel</a>), the UK, Canada and other countries. The <a href="/wiki/Peshawar" title="Peshawar">Peshawar</a> Jewish community ceased to exist<sup id="cite_ref-Pakistan_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pakistan-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> although a small community reportedly still exists in <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>.
</p><p>A substantial number of people in Pakistan believe that the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on the World Trade Center in New York were a secret Jewish conspiracy organized by Israel's <a href="/wiki/MOSSAD" class="mw-redirect" title="MOSSAD">MOSSAD</a>, as were the <a href="/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">7 July 2005 London bombings</a>, allegedly perpetrated by Jews in order to discredit Muslims. Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Political_commentator" class="mw-redirect" title="Political commentator">political commentator</a> <a href="/wiki/Zaid_Hamid" title="Zaid Hamid">Zaid Hamid</a> claimed that Indian Jews perpetrated the <a href="/wiki/2008_Mumbai_attacks" title="2008 Mumbai attacks">2008 Mumbai attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Such allegations echo traditional antisemitic theories.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
The Jewish religious movement of <a href="/wiki/Chabad_Lubavich" class="mw-redirect" title="Chabad Lubavich">Chabad Lubavich</a> had a <a href="/wiki/Nariman_House" title="Nariman House">mission house</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> that was attacked in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Mumbai_attacks" title="2008 Mumbai attacks">2008 Mumbai attacks</a>, perpetrated by militants connected to Pakistan led by <a href="/wiki/Ajmal_Kasab" title="Ajmal Kasab">Ajmal Kasab</a>, a Pakistani national.<sup id="cite_ref-PakAdmitsNYT_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PakAdmitsNYT-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">Antisemitic</a> intents were evident from the testimonies of Kasab following his arrest and trial.<sup id="cite_ref-Rubenstein2011_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rubenstein2011-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Antisemitism in Saudi Arabia">Antisemitism in Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="History of the Jews in Saudi Arabia">History of the Jews in Saudi Arabia</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saudi-Arabian_textbook_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi-Arabian textbook controversy">Saudi textbooks</a> vilify Jews, call Jews apes; demand that students avoid and not befriend Jews; claim that Jews worship the devil; and encourage Muslims to engage in <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">Jihad</a> to vanquish Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
Saudi Arabian government officials and state religious leaders often promote the idea that Jews are conspiring to take over the entire world; as proof of their claims they publish and frequently cite <i>The Protocols of the Elders of Zion</i> as factual.<sup id="cite_ref-CMIP-KSA2001_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMIP-KSA2001-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, the official Saudi Arabia tourism website said that Jews and holders of Israeli passports would not be issued visas to enter the country. After an uproar, the restriction against Jews was removed from the website although the ban against Israeli passport-holders remained.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> In late 2014, a Saudi newspaper reported that foreign workers of most religions, including Judaism, were welcome in the kingdom, but Israeli citizens were not.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Turkey" title="Antisemitism in Turkey">Antisemitism in Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Turkey" title="History of the Jews in Turkey">History of the Jews in Turkey</a></div>
<p>In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Neve_Shalom_Synagogue" title="Neve Shalom Synagogue">Neve Shalom Synagogue</a> was targeted in a car bombing, killing 21 Turkish Muslims and 6 Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2011, the <i>Economist</i> suggested that "The best way for Turks to promote democracy would be to vote against the ruling party". Not long after, the Turkish Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a>, said that "The International media, as they are supported by Israel, would not be happy with the continuation of the AKP government".<sup id="cite_ref-cm_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cm-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Hurriyet Daily News</i> quoted Erdoğan at the time as claiming "The Economist is part of an Israeli conspiracy that aims to topple the Turkish government".<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
Moreover, during Erdogan's tenure, Hitler's <i><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i> has once again become a best selling book in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-cm_288-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cm-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Prime Minister Erdogan called antisemitism a "crime against humanity." He also said that "as a minority, they're our citizens. Both their security and the right to observe their faith are under our guarantee."<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neoantisemismo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Neoantisemismo.jpg/220px-Neoantisemismo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Neoantisemismo.jpg/330px-Neoantisemismo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Neoantisemismo.jpg/440px-Neoantisemismo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1994" data-file-height="1202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neoantisemismo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Antisemitic graffiti equating Judaism with Nazism and money, found in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Europe" title="Antisemitism in Europe">Antisemitism in Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_antisemitism" title="New antisemitism">New antisemitism</a></div>
<p>According to a 2004 report from the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Center_for_Public_Affairs" title="Jerusalem Center for Public Affairs">Jerusalem Center for Public Affairs</a>, antisemitism had increased significantly in Europe since 2000, with significant increases in verbal attacks against Jews and vandalism such as graffiti, fire bombings of Jewish schools, desecration of synagogues and cemeteries. Germany, France, Britain, and Russia are the countries with the highest rate of antisemitic incidents in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-mgjmsp_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgjmsp-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The Netherlands and Sweden have also consistently had high rates of antisemitic attacks since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some claim that recent European antisemitic violence can actually be seen as a spillover from the long running <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab-Israeli conflict</a> since the majority of the perpetrators are from the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Europe" title="Islam in Europe">large Muslim immigrant communities in European cities</a>. However, compared to France, the United Kingdom and much of the rest of Europe, in Germany Arab and pro-Palestinian groups are involved in only a small percentage of antisemitic incidents.<sup id="cite_ref-mgjmsp_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgjmsp-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The Stephen Roth Institute for the Study of Contemporary Antisemitism and Racism</i>, most of the more extreme attacks on Jewish sites and physical attacks on Jews in Europe come from militant Islamic and Muslim groups, and most Jews tend to be assaulted in countries where groups of young Muslim immigrants reside.<sup id="cite_ref-roth_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roth-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 January 2006, Britain's chief <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">rabbi</a>, Lord <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Sacks" title="Jonathan Sacks">Jonathan Sacks</a>, warned that what he called a "tsunami of antisemitism" was spreading globally. In an interview with <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a>, Sacks said: "A number of my rabbinical colleagues throughout Europe have been assaulted and attacked on the streets. We've had synagogues desecrated. We've had Jewish schools burnt to the ground—not here but in France. People are attempting to silence and even ban Jewish societies on campuses on the grounds that Jews must support the state of Israel, therefore they should be banned, which is quite extraordinary because... British Jews see themselves as British citizens. So it's that kind of feeling that you don't know what's going to happen next that's making... some European Jewish communities uncomfortable."<sup id="cite_ref-Gillan_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillan-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following an escalation in antisemitism in 2012, which included the <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_and_Montauban_shootings" title="Toulouse and Montauban shootings">deadly shooting of three children</a> at a Jewish school in France, the <a href="/wiki/European_Jewish_Congress" title="European Jewish Congress">European Jewish Congress</a> demanded in July a more proactive response. EJC President Moshe Kantor explained, "We call on authorities to take a more proactive approach so there would be no reason for statements of regret and denunciation. All these smaller attacks remind me of smaller tremors before a massive earthquake. The Jewish community cannot afford to be subject to an earthquake and the authorities cannot say that the writing was not on the wall." He added that European countries should take legislative efforts to ban any form of <a href="/wiki/Incitement" title="Incitement">incitement</a>, as well as to equip the authorities with the necessary tools to confront any attempt to expand <a href="/wiki/Terrorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrorist">terrorist</a> and violent activities against Jewish communities in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-EJP_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJP-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_contemporary_Austria" title="Antisemitism in contemporary Austria">Antisemitism in contemporary Austria</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_21st-century_France" title="Antisemitism in 21st-century France">Antisemitism in 21st-century France</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_France" title="History of the Jews in France">History of the Jews in France</a></div>
<p>France is home to the continent's largest Jewish community (about 600,000). Jewish leaders decry an intensifying antisemitism in France,<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> mainly among Muslims of <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> or African heritage, but also growing among <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> islanders from former French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Former Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> denounced the killing of <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Halimi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilan Halimi">Ilan Halimi</a> on 13 February 2006 as an antisemitic crime.
</p><p>Jewish philanthropist Baron <a href="/wiki/Eric_de_Rothschild" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric de Rothschild">Eric de Rothschild</a> suggests that the extent of antisemitism in France has been exaggerated. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i> he says that "the one thing you can't say is that France is an anti-Semitic country."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg/220px-Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg/330px-Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg/440px-Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4978" data-file-height="3435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toulouse_-_Drapeaux_en_bernes_place_du_Capitole_-_2012-03-22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mourning<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> flags of the European Union, France and Midi-Pyrénées on the <a href="/wiki/Capitole_de_Toulouse" title="Capitole de Toulouse">Capitole de Toulouse</a> after the antisemitic attacks.</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2012, Mohammed Merah <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_and_Montauban_shootings" title="Toulouse and Montauban shootings">opened fire at a Jewish school</a> in Toulouse, killing a teacher and three children. An 8-year-old girl was shot in the head at point blank range. President <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> said that it was "obvious" it was an antisemitic attack<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> and that, "I want to say to all the leaders of the Jewish community, how close we feel to them. All of France is by their side." The Israeli Prime Minister condemned the "despicable anti-Semitic" murders.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> After a 32-hour siege and standoff with the police outside his house, and a French raid, Merah jumped off a balcony and was shot in the head and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> Merah told police during the standoff that he intended to keep on attacking, and he loved death the way the police loved life. He also claimed connections with al-Qaeda.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>4 months later, in July 2012, a French Jewish teenager wearing a "distinctive religious symbol" was the victim of a violent antisemitic attack on a train travelling between Toulouse and Lyon. The teen was first verbally harassed and later beaten up by two assailants. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Prasquier" title="Richard Prasquier">Richard Prasquier</a> from the French Jewish umbrella group, <a href="/wiki/Conseil_Repr%C3%A9sentatif_des_Institutions_juives_de_France" title="Conseil Représentatif des Institutions juives de France">CRIF</a>, called the attack "another development in the worrying trend of anti-Semitism in our country."<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another incident in July 2012 dealt with the vandalism of the synagogue of <a href="/wiki/Noisy-le-Grand" title="Noisy-le-Grand">Noisy-le-Grand</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Seine-Saint-Denis">Seine-Saint-Denis</a> district in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. The synagogue was vandalized three times in a ten-day period. Prayer books and shawls were thrown on the floor, windows were shattered, drawers were ransacked, and walls, tables, clocks, and floors were vandalized. The authorities were alerted of the incidents by the Bureau National de Vigilance Contre L'Antisémtisme (BNVCA), a French antisemitism watchdog group, which called for more measures to be taken to prevent future hate crimes. BNVCA President Sammy Ghozlan stated that, "Despite the measures taken, things persist, and I think that we need additional legislation, because the Jewish community is annoyed."<sup id="cite_ref-Algemeiner1_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Algemeiner1-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2012, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Cooper" title="Abraham Cooper">Abraham Cooper</a>, the dean of the <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a>, met French Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Valls" title="Manuel Valls">Manuel Valls</a> and reported that antisemitic attacks against French Jews increased by 40% since <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_and_Montauban_shootings" title="Toulouse and Montauban shootings">Merah's shooting spree</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>. Cooper pressed Valls to take extra measures to secure the safety of French Jews, as well as to discuss strategies to foil an increasing trend of lone-wolf terrorists on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-IHA_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHA-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg/300px-Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg/450px-Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/06/Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="502" data-file-height="341" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stab-in-the-back_postcard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An illustration from a 1919 Austrian postcard showing a <a href="/wiki/Caricature" title="Caricature">caricatured</a> <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jew</a> stabbing the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">German Army</a> in the back with a dagger during <a href="/wiki/WWI" class="mw-redirect" title="WWI">WWI</a>. The capitulation was blamed upon the unpatriotic populace, the <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">Socialists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>, and especially the Jews.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Germany" title="History of the Jews in Germany">History of the Jews in Germany</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Sch%C3%A4uble" title="Wolfgang Schäuble">Wolfgang Schäuble</a>, the Interior Minister of Germany in 2006, pointed out the official policy of Germany: "We will not tolerate any form of extremism, xenophobia or anti-Semitism."<sup id="cite_ref-bbcwolfgang_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcwolfgang-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> Although the number of extreme right-wing groups and organisations grew from 141 (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt1_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt1-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> to 182 (2006),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt2_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt2-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> especially in the formerly communist East Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-bbcwolfgang_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcwolfgang-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fight_Against_The_Right" class="mw-redirect" title="Fight Against The Right">Germany's measures against right-wing groups</a> and antisemitism are effective, despite Germany having the highest rates of antisemitic acts in Europe. According to the annual reports of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesamt_f%C3%BCr_Verfassungsschutz" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesamt für Verfassungsschutz">Federal Office for the Protection of the Constitution</a> the overall number of far-right extremists in Germany dropped during the last years from 49,700 (2001),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt1_311-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt1-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> 45,000 (2002),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt1_311-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt1-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> 41,500 (2003),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt1_311-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt1-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> 40,700 (2004),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt2_312-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt2-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> 39,000 (2005),<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt2_312-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt2-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> to 38,600 in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-bundesamt2_312-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesamt2-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Germany provided several million euros to fund "nationwide programs aimed at fighting far-right extremism, including teams of traveling consultants, and victims' groups."<sup id="cite_ref-ihtassociated_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ihtassociated-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2012, two women were assaulted in Germany, sprayed with tear gas, and were shown a "<a href="/wiki/Nazi_salute" title="Nazi salute">Hitler salute</a>," apparently because of a <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a> necklace that they wore.<sup id="cite_ref-Frauen_im_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frauen_im-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late August 2012, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> police investigated an attack on a 53-year-old rabbi and his 6-year-old daughter, allegedly by four Arab teens, after which the rabbi needed treatment for head wounds at a hospital. The police classified the attack as a hate crime. <i>Jüdische Allgemeine</i> reported that the rabbi was wearing a <a href="/wiki/Kippah" title="Kippah">kippah</a> and was approached by one of the teens, who asked the rabbi if he was Jewish. The teen then attacked the rabbi while yelling antisemitic comments, and threatened to kill the rabbi's daughter. Berlin's mayor condemned the attack, saying that "Berlin is an international city in which intolerance, xenophobia and anti-Semitism are not being tolerated. Police will undertake all efforts to find and arrest the perpetrators."<sup id="cite_ref-VoNG_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VoNG-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2012, various historians, including Dr. Julius H. Schoeps, a prominent German-Jewish historian and a member of the German Interior Ministry's commission to combat antisemitism, charged the majority of <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a> deputies with failing to understand antisemitism and the imperativeness of periodic legislative reports on German antisemitism. Schoeps cited various antisemitic statements by German parliament members as well. The report in question determined that 15% of Germans are antisemitic while over 20% espouse "latent anti-Semitism," but the report has been criticized for downplaying the sharpness of antisemitism in Germany, as well as for failing to examine anti-Israel media coverage in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Greece" title="Antisemitism in Greece">Antisemitism in Greece</a></div>
<p>Antisemitism in Greece manifests itself in religious, political and media discourse. The recent <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">Greek government-debt crisis</a> has facilitated the rise of far right groups in Greece, most notably the formerly obscure <a href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a>.
Jews have lived in Greece since antiquity, but the largest community of around 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> settled in <a href="/wiki/Thessalonica" class="mw-redirect" title="Thessalonica">Thessalonica</a> after an invitation from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Sultan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Sultan">Ottoman Sultan</a> in the 15th century. After Thessalonica was annexed to Greece in 1913, the Greek government recognized Jews as Greek citizens with full rights and attributed Judaism the status of a recognized and protected religion. Currently in Greece, Jewish communities representing the 5,000 Greek Jews are legal entities under public law. 
According to the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">ADL</a> (Anti-Defamation League) report of 2015, the "ADL Global 100", a report of the status of antisemitism in 100 countries around the world, 69% of the adult population in Greece harbor antisemitic attitudes and 85% think that "Jews have too much power in the business world".<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>
In March 2015, a survey about the Greeks' perceptions of the holocaust was published. Its findings showed that less than 60 percent of the respondents think that holocaust teaching should be included in the curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_contemporary_Hungary" title="Antisemitism in contemporary Hungary">Antisemitism in contemporary Hungary</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg/150px-Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg/225px-Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg/300px-Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jobbik-NewHungarianGuard-May2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the New Hungarian Guard stand at a Jobbik rally against a gathering of the <a href="/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress" title="World Jewish Congress">World Jewish Congress</a> in Budapest, 4 May 2013</div></div></div>
<p>In the 21st century, antisemitism in Hungary has evolved and received an institutional framework, while verbal and physical aggression against Jews has escalated, creating a great difference between its earlier manifestations in the 1990s and recent developments. One of the major representatives of this institutionalized antisemitic ideology is the popular Hungarian party <a href="/wiki/Jobbik" title="Jobbik">Jobbik</a>, which received 17 percent of the vote in the April 2010 national election. The far-right subculture, which ranges from nationalist shops to radical-nationalist and neo-Nazi festivals and events, plays a major role in the institutionalization of Hungarian antisemitism in the 21st century. The contemporary antisemitic rhetoric has been updated and expanded, but is still based on the old antisemitic notions. The traditional accusations and motifs include such phrases as Jewish occupation, international Jewish conspiracy, Jewish responsibility for the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>, Judeo-Bolshevism, as well as blood libels against Jews. Nevertheless, the past few years have seen the reemergence of the blood libel and an increase in Holocaust relativization and denial, while the monetary crisis has revived references to the "Jewish banker class".<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_21st-century_Italy" title="Antisemitism in 21st-century Italy">Antisemitism in 21st-century Italy</a></div>
<p>The ongoing political conflict between Israel and Palestine has played an important role in the development and expression of <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_21st_century" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitism in the 21st century">antisemitism in the 21st century</a>, and in Italy as well. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a>, which began in late September 2000, has set in motion unexpected mechanisms, whereby traditional anti-Jewish prejudices were mixed with politically based stereotypes.<sup id="cite_ref-EUMC_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUMC-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> In this belief system, Israeli Jews were charged with full responsibility for the fate of the peace process and with the conflict presented as embodying the struggle between good (the Palestinians) and evil (the Israeli Jews).<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">History of the Jews in the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> has the second highest incidence of antisemitic incidents in the European Union. However, it is difficult to obtain exact figures because the specific groups against whom attacks are made are not specifically identified in police reports, and analyses of police data for antisemitism therefore relies on key-word searches, e.g. "Jew" or "Israel". According to Centre for Information and Documentation on Israel (CIDI), a pro-Israel lobby group in the Netherlands,<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> the number of antisemitic incidents reported in the whole of the Netherlands was 108 in 2008, 93 in 2009, and 124 in 2010. Some two thirds of this are acts of aggression. There are approximately 52 000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Dutch Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> According to the NRC Handelsblad newspaper, the number of antisemitic incidents in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> was 14 in 2008 and 30 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Raphaël Evers, an <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_judaism" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox judaism">orthodox</a> rabbi in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, told the <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a> newspaper <a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a> that Jews can no longer be safe in the city anymore due to the risk of violent assaults. "We Jews no longer feel at home here in the Netherlands. Many people talk about moving to Israel," he said.<sup id="cite_ref-aftenposten.no_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aftenposten.no-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank_Foundation" title="Anne Frank Foundation">Anne Frank Foundation</a>, antisemitism in the Netherlands in 2011 was roughly at the same level as in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> Actual antisemitic incidents increased from 19 in 2010 to 30 in 2011. Verbal antisemitic incidents dropped slightly from 1173 in 2010 to 1098 in 2011. This accounts for 75%–80% of all verbal racist incidents in the Netherlands. Antisemitism is more prevalent in the age group 23–27 years, which is a younger group than that of racist incidents in general.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Norway" title="Antisemitism in Norway">Antisemitism in Norway</a></div>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Broadcasting_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Broadcasting Corporation">Norwegian Broadcasting Corporation</a> after one year of research, revealed that antisemitism was common among some 8th, 9th, and 10th graders in Oslo's schools. Teachers at schools with large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> revealed that Muslim students often "praise or admire Adolf Hitler for his killing of <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a>", that "Jew-hate is legitimate within vast groups of Muslim students" and that "Muslims laugh or command [teachers] to stop when trying to educate about the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>". Additionally, "while some students might protest when some express support for <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>, none object when students express hate of Jews", saying that it says in "the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> that you shall kill Jews, all true Muslims hate Jews". Most of these students were said to be born and raised in Norway. One <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jewish</a> father also stated that his child had been taken by a Muslim mob after school (though the child managed to escape), reportedly "to be taken out to the forest and <a href="/wiki/Lynching" title="Lynching">hung</a> because he was a Jew".<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Norwegian Education Minister Kristin Halvorsen referred to the antisemitism reported in this study as being "completely unacceptable." The head of a local Islamic council joined Jewish leaders and Halvorsen in denouncing such antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-Operation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Co-Operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-Operation in Europe</a> issued a report regarding antisemitism in Norway, criticizing Norway for an increase in antisemitism in the country and blaming Norwegian officials for failing to address antisemitism."<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG/375px-Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG" decoding="async" width="375" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG/563px-Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG/750px-Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3496" data-file-height="1065" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Sukiennice_001.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The sale of stereotypical figures of Jews, including <a href="/wiki/Jew_with_a_coin" title="Jew with a coin">Jew with a coin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Żyd z pieniążkiem</i>), <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Cloth_Hall" title="Kraków Cloth Hall">Kraków Cloth Hall</a>, 2009</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a>'s study in 2016 found that 37% of surveyed Poles expressed negative attitudes towards Jews (up from 32% in 2015); 56% said that they wouldn't accept a Jew in their family (up from 46%); and 32% wouldn't want Jewish neighbors (up from 27%).<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2015, following Antoni Macierewicz's (<a href="/wiki/Law_and_Justice" title="Law and Justice">Law and Justice</a> party) designation as Minister of National Defence, he faced allegations of antisemitism and protests by the <a href="/wiki/Anti_Defamation_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti Defamation League">Anti Defamation League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-antisemitism_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antisemitism-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sokol01_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sokol01-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2018, the Polish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mateusz_Morawiecki" title="Mateusz Morawiecki">Mateusz Morawiecki</a> stated that "there were Jewish perpetrators" of the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, "not only German perpetrators."<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Lauder" title="Ronald Lauder">Ronald Lauder</a>, the president of the <a href="/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress" title="World Jewish Congress">World Jewish Congress</a>, condemned Morawiecki's words: "This is nothing short of an attempt to falsify history, that is one of the very worst forms of anti-Semitism and Holocaust obfuscation."<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> Israeli politician <a href="/wiki/Yair_Lapid" title="Yair Lapid">Yair Lapid</a>, head of the centrist <a href="/wiki/Yesh_Atid" title="Yesh Atid">Yesh Atid</a> party, said Morawiecki's remark is "anti-Semitism of the oldest kind."<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Russia" title="Antisemitism in Russia">Antisemitism in Russia</a></div>
<p>Since the early 2000s, levels of antisemitism in Russia have been low, and steadily decreasing.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-feor_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feor-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> President of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Jewish_Congress" title="Russian Jewish Congress">Russian Jewish Congress</a> attributes this in part to the vanished state sponsorship of antisemitism. At the same time experts warn that worsening economic conditions may lead to the surge of <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a> and antisemitism in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Spain" title="Antisemitism in Spain">Antisemitism in Spain</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Sweden" title="Antisemitism in Sweden">Antisemitism in Sweden</a></div>
<p>After Germany and Austria, Sweden has the highest rate of antisemitic incidents in Europe, though the Netherlands has reported a higher rate of antisemitism in some years.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> A government study in 2006 estimated that 15% of Swedes agree with the statement: "The Jews have too much influence in the world today".<sup id="cite_ref-GovStudy_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovStudy-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> 5% of the total adult population and 39% of adult Muslims "harbour systematic antisemitic views".<sup id="cite_ref-GovStudy_341-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovStudy-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> The former prime minister <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ran_Persson" title="Göran Persson">Göran Persson</a> described these results as "surprising and terrifying". However, the rabbi of Stockholm's Orthodox Jewish community, Meir Horden, said that "It's not true to say that the Swedes are anti-Semitic. Some of them are hostile to Israel because they support the weak side, which they perceive the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinians</a> to be."<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, a synagogue that served the Jewish community in Malmö was set ablaze. Jewish cemeteries were repeatedly desecrated, worshippers were abused while returning home from prayer, and masked men mockingly chanted "Hitler" in the streets. As a result of security concerns, Malmö's synagogue has guards and rocket-proof glass in the windows, and the Jewish kindergarten can only be reached through thick steel security doors.<sup id="cite_ref-Malmo_Jews_leaving_Telegraph_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malmo_Jews_leaving_Telegraph-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2010, the Swedish publication <i>The Local</i> published series of articles about the growing antisemitism in <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6,_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Malmö, Sweden">Malmö, Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the Malmö police received reports of 79 antisemitic incidents, which was twice the number of the previous year (2008).<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> Fredrik Sieradzki, spokesman for the Malmö Jewish community, estimated that the already small Jewish population is shrinking by 5% a year. "Malmö is a place to move away from," he said, citing antisemitism as the primary reason.<sup id="cite_ref-forward.com_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forward.com-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> In March 2010, Fredrik Sieradzk told <i>Die Presse</i>, an Austrian Internet publication, that Jews are being "harassed and physically attacked" by "people from the Middle East," although he added that only a small number of Malmö's 40,000 Muslims "exhibit hatred of Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> In October 2010, <i>The Forward</i> reported on the current state of Jews and the level of antisemitism in Sweden. Henrik Bachner, a writer and professor of history at the University of Lund, claimed that members of the Swedish Parliament have attended anti-Israel rallies where the Israeli flag was burned while the flags of Hamas and Hezbollah were waved, and the rhetoric was often antisemitic—not just anti-Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-moveaway_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moveaway-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> Judith Popinski, an 86-year-old Holocaust survivor, stated that she is no longer invited to schools that have a large Muslim presence to tell her story of surviving the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-forward.com_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forward.com-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> In December 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> organization <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a> issued a travel advisory concerning Sweden, advising Jews to express "extreme caution" when visiting the southern parts of the country due to an alleged increase in verbal and physical harassment of Jewish citizens in the city of <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malmö">Malmö</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ilmar_Reepalu" title="Ilmar Reepalu">Ilmar Reepalu</a>, the mayor of Malmö for over 15 years, has been accused of failing to protect the Jewish community in Malmö, causing 30 Jewish families to leave the city in 2010, and more preparing to leave, which has left the possibility that Malmö's Jewish community will disappear soon. Critics of Reepalu say that his statements, such as antisemitism in Malmö actually being an "understandable" consequence of Israeli policy in the Middle East, have encouraged young Muslims to abuse and harass the Jewish community.<sup id="cite_ref-Malmo_Jews_leaving_Telegraph_343-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malmo_Jews_leaving_Telegraph-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i>the Sunday Telegraph</i> in February 2010, Reepalu said, "There haven't been any attacks on Jewish people, and if Jews from the city want to move to Israel that is not a matter for Malmö," which renewed concerns about Reepalu.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Ukraine" title="Antisemitism in Ukraine">Antisemitism in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg/220px-Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg/330px-Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg/440px-Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antisemithic_graffiti_Lvov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Antisemithic graffiti in <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Yids" class="mw-redirect" title="Yids">Yids</a> will not reside in Lviv</i>, 2007</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oleh_Tyahnybok" title="Oleh Tyahnybok">Oleh Tyahnybok</a>, the leader of the far-right <a href="/wiki/Svoboda_(political_party)" title="Svoboda (political party)">Svoboda</a> party, whose members hold senior positions in <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet of Ukraine">Ukraine's government</a>, urged his party to fight "the Moscow-Jewish mafia ruling Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Algemeiner Journal</i> reported: "Svoboda supporters include among their heroes leaders of pro-Nazi World War II organizations known for their <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Ukraine" title="The Holocaust in Ukraine">atrocities against Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia" title="Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia">Poles</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists</a> (OUN), the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army" title="Ukrainian Insurgent Army">Ukrainian Insurgent Army</a> (UPA), and the <a href="/wiki/14th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Ukrainian)" class="mw-redirect" title="14th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Ukrainian)">14th Waffen-SS Galicia Division</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/The_Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="The Simon Wiesenthal Center">The Simon Wiesenthal Center</a> (in January 2011) "Ukraine has, to the best of our knowledge, never conducted a single investigation of a local Nazi war criminal, let alone prosecuted a Holocaust perpetrator."<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <i>Der Spiegel</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dmytro_Yarosh" title="Dmytro Yarosh">Dmytro Yarosh</a>, leader of the far-right <a href="/wiki/Right_Sector" title="Right Sector">Right Sector</a>, wrote: "I wonder how it came to pass that most of the billionaires in Ukraine are Jews?"<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> Late February 2014 Yarosh pledged during a meeting with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>'s ambassador in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> to fight all forms of racism.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> Right Sector's leader for West Ukraine, <a href="/wiki/Oleksandr_Muzychko" title="Oleksandr Muzychko">Oleksandr Muzychko</a>, has talked about fighting "communists, Jews and Russians for as long as blood flows in my veins."<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> Muzychko was shot dead on 24 March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcPoliceRaid_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcPoliceRaid-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> An official inquiry concluded he had shot himself in the heart at the end of a chase with the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian police">Ukrainian police</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcPoliceRaid_358-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcPoliceRaid-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2014, <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a> Chief Rabbi Pinchas Vishedski said that "Anti-Semitic incidents in the Russian-speaking east were rare, unlike in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> and western Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> In an April 2014 article about anti-Jewish violence in Ukraine in <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> no incidents outside this "Russian-speaking east" were mentioned.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the Israel's Ambassador to Ukraine, the antisemitism occurs here much less frequently than in other European countries, and has more a hooligan's nature rather than a system.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2017, Ukrainian politician <a href="/wiki/Nadiya_Savchenko" title="Nadiya Savchenko">Nadiya Savchenko</a>  said during a television interview that Jews held disproportionate control over Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> (SBU) senior officer Vasily Vovk wrote that Jews "aren't Ukrainians and I will destroy you along with [Ukrainian oligarch and Jewish lawmaker Vadim] <a href="/wiki/Vadim_Rabinovich" title="Vadim Rabinovich">Rabinovych</a>. I'm telling you one more time - go to hell, zhidi [kikes], the Ukrainian people have had it to here with you. Ukraine must be governed by Ukrainians."<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The antisemitism report for 2017 that Israel's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Diaspora_Affairs" title="Ministry of Diaspora Affairs">Ministry of Diaspora Affairs</a> under <a href="/wiki/Naftali_Bennett" title="Naftali Bennett">Naftali Bennett</a> published in January 2018 stated that "A striking exception in the trend of decrease in antisemitic incidents in Eastern Europe was Ukraine, where the number of recorded antisemitic attacks was doubled from last year and surpassed the tally for all the incidents reported throughout the entire region combined.".<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul style="width:100%;list-style:none;-webkit-column-width:12em;-moz-column-width:12em;column-width:12em;"><li><span style="padding:0 1em;background-color:#FFA6C9;border:1px solid #FFA6C9;margin-right:1em;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;">&#160;</span> 2004</li>
