<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Antisemitism in the United Kingdom">Antisemitism in the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Jews" title="British Jews">British Jews</a></div>
<p>In 2017 an <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Jewish_Policy_Research" title="Institute for Jewish Policy Research">Institute for Jewish Policy Research</a> survey found that the levels of antisemitism in Great Britain were among the lowest in the world, with 2.4% expressing multiple antisemitic attitudes, and about 70% having a favourable opinion of Jews. However, only 17% had a favourable opinion of Israel, with 33% holding an unfavourable view.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-20170913_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-20170913-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpr-201709_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpr-201709-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, a report by the Campaign Against Antisemitism (CAA) found that the previous year, 2016, had been the worst on record for antisemitic hate crime in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Campaign_Against_Antisemitism_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campaign_Against_Antisemitism-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Prior to that, 2015 had been the worst year on record, and 2014 was the worst year on record before that. The report found that in 2016, antisemitic crime rose by 15% compared to 2015, or 45% compared to 2014. It also found that 1 in 10 antisemitic crimes was violent. Despite rising levels of antisemitic crime, the report said there had been a decrease in the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_charge" title="Criminal charge">charging</a> of antisemitic crime. In the report's foreword, the CAA's Chairman wrote: "Britain has the political will to fight antisemitism and strong laws with which to do it, but those responsible for tackling the rapidly growing racist targeting of British Jews are failing to enforce the law. There is a very real danger of Jewish citizens emigrating, as has happened elsewhere in Europe unless there is radical change."<sup id="cite_ref-Campaign_Against_Antisemitism_372-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campaign_Against_Antisemitism-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Every year since 2015, the CAA has commissioned polling by <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a> concerning the attitude of the British public toward British Jews. In 2017, their polling found that 36% of British adults believed at least one of the antisemitic statements pollsters had shown them to be true, a reduction from 39% in 2016 and 45% in 2015. Additionally, the polling revealed widespread fear amongst British Jews, with almost 1 in 3 saying that they had considered emigrating in the last two years due to antisemitism, and 37% saying that they concealed their Judaism in public. The report gave various indications as to the cause of the fears, with British Jews identifying Islamist antisemitism, <a href="/wiki/Far-left_antisemitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Far-left antisemitism">far-left antisemitism</a> and far-right antisemitism as their main concerns, in that order. 78% of British Jews saying that they had witnessed antisemitism disguised as a political comment about Israel, 76% thoughts that political developments were contributing antisemitism, and 52% felt that the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Prosecution_Service" title="Crown Prosecution Service">Crown Prosecution Service</a> was not doing enough.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, a group of British <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Members of Parliament</a> set up an inquiry into antisemitism, which published its findings in 2006. Its report stated that "until recently, the prevailing opinion both within the Jewish community and beyond [had been] that antisemitism had receded to the point that it existed only on the margins of society." It found a reversal of this progress since 2000. The inquiry was reconstituted following a surge in antisemitic incidents in Britain during the summer of 2014, and the new inquiry published its report in 2015, making recommendations for reducing antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Home_Affairs_Select_Committee" title="Home Affairs Select Committee">Home Affairs Select Committee</a> held an inquiry into the rise of antisemitism in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> The inquiry called <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Farron" title="Tim Farron">Tim Farron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angus_Robertson" title="Angus Robertson">Angus Robertson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> and others to give evidence.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Canada" title="Antisemitism in Canada">Antisemitism in Canada</a></div>
<p>Although antisemitism in Canada is less prevalent than in many other countries, there have been recent incidents. For example, a 2004 study identified 24 incidents of antisemitism between 14 March and 14 July 2004 in Newfoundland, Montreal, Quebec City, Ottawa, the Greater Toronto Area (GTA), and some smaller Ontario communities. The incidents included vandalism and other attacks on four synagogues, six cemeteries, four schools, and a number of businesses and private residences.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_United_States" title="Antisemitism in the United States">Antisemitism in the United States</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_antisemitism_in_the_United_States" title="History of antisemitism in the United States">History of antisemitism in the United States</a></div>
<p>In November 2005, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Commission_on_Civil_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Commission on Civil Rights">U.S. Commission on Civil Rights</a> examined antisemitism on college campuses. It reported that "incidents of threatened bodily injury, physical intimidation or property damage are now rare", but antisemitism still occurs on many campuses and is a "serious problem." The Commission recommended that the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Education">U.S. Department of Education</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Office_for_Civil_Rights" title="Office for Civil Rights">Office for Civil Rights</a> protect college students from antisemitism through vigorous enforcement of <i>Title VI</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> and further recommended that <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> clarify that Title VI applies to discrimination against Jewish students.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 September 2006, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Yale_Initiative_for_the_Interdisciplinary_Study_of_Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Yale Initiative for the Interdisciplinary Study of Anti-Semitism">Yale Initiative for the Interdisciplinary Study of Anti-Semitism</a> (YIISA), the first North American university-based center for study of the subject, as part of its Institution for Social and Policy Studies. Director <a href="/wiki/Charles_A._Small" title="Charles A. Small">Charles Small</a> of the Center cited the increase in antisemitism worldwide in recent years as generating a "need to understand the current manifestation of this disease".<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, Yale voted to close this initiative. After carrying out a routine review, the faculty review committee said that the initiative had not met its research and teaching standards. <a href="/wiki/Donald_Green" title="Donald Green">Donald Green</a>, then head of Yale's Institution for Social and Policy Studies, the body under whose aegis the antisemitism initiative was run, said that it had not had many papers published in the relevant leading journals or attracted many students. As with other programs that had been in a similar situation, the initiative had therefore been cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-nhregister201106_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhregister201106-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> This decision has been criticized by figures such as former U.S. Commission on Civil Rights Staff Director <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_L._Marcus" title="Kenneth L. Marcus">Kenneth L. Marcus</a>, who is now the director of the Initiative to Combat Anti-Semitism and Anti-Israelism in America's Educational Systems at the Institute for Jewish and Community Research, and <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Lipstadt" title="Deborah Lipstadt">Deborah Lipstadt</a>, who described the decision as "weird" and "strange."<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antony_Lerman" title="Antony Lerman">Antony Lerman</a> has supported Yale's decision, describing the YIISA as a politicized initiative that was devoted to the promotion of Israel rather than to serious research on antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2007 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> (ADL) concluded that 15% of Americans hold antisemitic views, which was in-line with the average of the previous ten years, but a decline from the 29% of the early sixties. The survey concluded that education was a strong predictor, "with most educated Americans being remarkably free of prejudicial views." The belief that Jews have too much power was considered a common antisemitic view by the ADL. Other views indicating antisemitism, according to the survey, include the view that Jews are more loyal to Israel than America, and that they are responsible for the death of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus of Nazareth</a>. The survey found that antisemitic Americans are likely to be intolerant generally, e.g. regarding immigration and free-speech. The 2007 survey also found that 29% of foreign-born <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanics</a> and 32% of <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African-Americans</a> hold strong antisemitic beliefs, three times more than the 10% for whites.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2009 study published in <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Review" title="Boston Review">Boston Review</a></i> found that nearly 25% of non-Jewish Americans blamed Jews for the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a>, with a higher percentage among Democrats than Republicans. 32% of Democrats blamed Jews for the financial crisis, versus 18% for Republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2012, the <a href="/wiki/California_state_assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="California state assembly">California state assembly</a> approved a <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding resolution</a> that "encourages university leaders to combat a wide array of anti-Jewish and anti-Israel actions," although the resolution "is purely symbolic and does not carry policy implications."<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico Magazine</a></i> published an article purporting to show links between U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> and the Jewish outreach organization <a href="/wiki/Chabad-Lubavitch" class="mw-redirect" title="Chabad-Lubavitch">Chabad-Lubavitch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup> The article was condemned, with the head of the Anti-Defamation League <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Greenblatt" title="Jonathan Greenblatt">Jonathan Greenblatt</a> saying that it "evokes age-old myths about Jews".<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2017, Jonathan Greenblatt, national director and CEO of the Anti-Defamation League, stated in an interview, "While anti-Semitic attitudes have remained consistent at 14%... anti-Semitic incidents have been on the rise. In 2016 we saw a 34% increase over the prior year in acts of harassment, vandalism, or violence directed at Jewish individuals and institutions. During the first three quarters of 2017, there was a 67% increase over the same period in 2016. We've seen double the number of incidents in K-12 schools, and almost a 60% increase on college campuses." <sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 29, 2018, an antisemitic terrorist <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_synagogue_shooting" title="Pittsburgh synagogue shooting">attacked the Tree of Life Synagogue</a> in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 25, 2019, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> international edition included a cartoon featuring U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> and Israeli PM <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>. Trump was shown wearing a <a href="/wiki/Kippah" title="Kippah">kippah</a> and Netanyahu was displayed as Trump's dog wearing a collar with the <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> After criticism from public and religious figures, <i>The Times</i> admitted to using "anti-Semitic tropes".<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup> On April 29, <i>The New York Times</i> came under scrutiny again for publishing another anti-Semitic cartoon featuring PM Netanyahu.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg/220px-Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg/330px-Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg/440px-Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg 2x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="404" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_in_Venezuela.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Antisemitic graffiti in Venezuela, alongside a <a href="/wiki/Hammer_and_sickle" title="Hammer and sickle">hammer and sickle</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Venezuela" title="Antisemitism in Venezuela">Antisemitism in Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Venezuela" title="History of the Jews in Venezuela">History of the Jews in Venezuela</a></div>
<p>In a 2009 news story, Michael Rowan and Douglas E. Schoen wrote, "In an infamous Christmas Eve speech several years ago, Chávez said the Jews killed Christ and have been gobbling up wealth and causing poverty and injustice worldwide ever since."<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a> stated that "[t]he world is for all of us, then, but it so happens that a minority, the descendants of the same ones that crucified Christ, the descendants of the same ones that kicked <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Bolívar</a> out of here and also crucified him in their own way over there in Santa Marta, in Colombia. A minority has taken possession of all of the wealth of the world."<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2012, opposition candidate for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Venezuelan_presidential_election" title="2012 Venezuelan presidential election">2012 Venezuelan presidential election</a> <a href="/wiki/Henrique_Capriles" title="Henrique Capriles">Henrique Capriles</a> was subject to what foreign journalists characterized as vicious<sup id="cite_ref-ChavezRival_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezRival-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> attacks by state-run media sources.<sup id="cite_ref-ChavezMedia_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezMedia-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheMan_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheMan-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall Street Journal">Wall Street Journal</a></i> said that Capriles "was vilified in a campaign in Venezuela's state-run media, which insinuated he was, among other things, a homosexual and a Zionist agent".<sup id="cite_ref-ChavezRival_402-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezRival-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> A 13 February 2012 opinion article in the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Radio_Nacional_de_Venezuela" title="Radio Nacional de Venezuela">Radio Nacional de Venezuela</a>, titled "The Enemy is Zionism"<sup id="cite_ref-ADL17022012_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADL17022012-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup> attacked Capriles' Jewish ancestry and linked him with Jewish national groups because of a meeting he had held with local Jewish leaders,<sup id="cite_ref-ChavezRival_402-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezRival-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChavezMedia_403-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezMedia-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JewishGay_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JewishGay-406">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup> saying, "This is our enemy, the Zionism that Capriles today represents... Zionism, along with capitalism, are responsible for 90% of world poverty and imperialist wars."<sup id="cite_ref-ChavezRival_402-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChavezRival-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Hess, Jonathan M. (Winter 2000). "Johann David Michaelis and the Colonial Imaginary: Orientalism and the Emergence of Racial Antisemitism in Eighteenth-Century Germany". <i>Jewish Social Studies</i>. <b>6</b> (2): 56–101. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1353%2Fjss.2000.0003">10.1353/jss.2000.0003</a>. <q>When the term "antisemitism" was first introduced in Germany in the late 1870s, those who used it did so in order to stress the radical difference between their own "antisemitism" and earlier forms of antagonism toward Jews and Judaism.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Jewish+Social+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=Johann+David+Michaelis+and+the+Colonial+Imaginary%3A+Orientalism+and+the+Emergence+of+Racial+Antisemitism+in+Eighteenth-Century+Germany&amp;rft.ssn=winter&amp;rft.volume=6&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=56-101&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1353%2Fjss.2000.0003&amp;rft.aulast=Hess&amp;rft.aufirst=Jonathan+M.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Marr" title="Wilhelm Marr">Marr, Wilhelm</a>. <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/Marr-Wilhelm-Der-Sieg-des-Judenthums-ueber-das-Germanenthum-2-2">Der Sieg des Judenthums über das Germanenthum. Vom nicht confessionellen Standpunkt aus betrachtet</a></i>. Rudolph Costenoble. 1879, 8th edition/printing. Archive.org. Marr uses the word "Semitismus" (Semitism) on pages 7, 11, 14, 30, 32, and 46; for example, one finds in the conclusion the following passage: "Ja, ich bin überzeutgt, ich habe ausgesprochen, was Millionen Juden im Stillen denken: Dem Semitismus gehört die Weltherrschaft!" (Yes, I am convinced that I have articulated what millions of Jews are quietly thinking: World domination belongs to Semitism!) (p. 46).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Marr" title="Wilhelm Marr">Marr, Wilhem</a> (1879). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.kevinmacdonald.net/Marr-Text-English.pdf">"The Victory of Judaism over Germanism: Viewed from a Nonreligious Point of View"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Translated by Rohringer, Gerhard<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 October</span> 2018</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+Victory+of+Judaism+over+Germanism%3A+Viewed+from+a+Nonreligious+Point+of+View&amp;rft.date=1879&amp;rft.aulast=Marr&amp;rft.aufirst=Wilhem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.kevinmacdonald.net%2FMarr-Text-English.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/wilhelm-marr">"Wilhelm Marr"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Jewish_Virtual_Library" title="Jewish Virtual Library">Jewish Virtual Library</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 October</span> 2018</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Jewish+Virtual+Library&amp;rft.atitle=Wilhelm+Marr&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.jewishvirtuallibrary.org%2Fwilhelm-marr&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-MZ1987-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-MZ1987_25-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-MZ1987_25-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Zimmermann, Moshe (1987). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=tYW013SjKM4C&amp;pg=PA112"><i>Wilhelm Marr: The Patriarch of Anti-Semitism</i></a>. Oxford University Press. p.&#160;112. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-536495-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-536495-8"><bdi>978-0-19-536495-8</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 October</span> 2018</span>. <q>The term "anti-Semitism" was unsuitable from the beginning for the real essence of Jew-hatred, which remained anchored, more or less, in the Christian tradition even when it moved via the natural sciences, into racism. It is doubtful whether the term which was first publicizes in an institutional context (the Anti-Semitic League) would have appeared at all if the "Anti-Chancellor League," which fought Bismarck's policy, had not been in existence since 1875. The founders of the new Organization adopted the elements of "anti" and "league," and searched for the proper term: Marr exchanged the term "Jew" for "Semite" which he already favored. It is possible that the shortened form "Sem" is used with such frequency and ease by Marr (and in his writings) due to its literary advantage and because it reminded Marr of Sem Biedermann, his Jewish employer from the Vienna period.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Wilhelm+Marr%3A+The+Patriarch+of+Anti-Semitism&amp;rft.pages=112&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1987&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-536495-8&amp;rft.aulast=Zimmermann&amp;rft.aufirst=Moshe&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DtYW013SjKM4C%26pg%3DPA112&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-IHRA1-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-IHRA1_31-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.holocaustremembrance.com/sites/default/files/memo-on-spelling-of-antisemitism_final-1.pdf">"Memo on Spelling of Antisemitism"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <a href="/wiki/International_Holocaust_Remembrance_Alliance" title="International Holocaust Remembrance Alliance">International Holocaust Remembrance Alliance</a>. April 2015. <q>...the hyphenated spelling allows for the possibility of something called ‘Semitism’, which not only legitimizes a form of pseudo- scientific racial classification that was thoroughly discredited by association with Nazi ideology, but also divides the term, stripping it from its meaning of opposition and hatred toward Jews.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Memo+on+Spelling+of+Antisemitism&amp;rft.pub=International+Holocaust+Remembrance+Alliance&amp;rft.date=2015-04&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.holocaustremembrance.com%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fmemo-on-spelling-of-antisemitism_final-1.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-IHRA2-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-IHRA2_32-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-IHRA2_32-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.holocaustremembrance.com/sites/default/files/memo-on-spelling-of-antisemitism_final-1.pdf">"Memo on Spelling of Antisemitism"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <a href="/wiki/International_Holocaust_Remembrance_Alliance" title="International Holocaust Remembrance Alliance">International Holocaust Remembrance Alliance</a>. <li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/James_Carroll_(author)" title="James Carroll (author)">Carroll, James</a> (2002). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=n7EUdvSQs70C&amp;pg=PT421"><i>Constantine's Sword: The Church and the Jews</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-Sevenster1975-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Sevenster1975_39-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Sevenster, Jan Nicolaas (1975). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=yLE3AAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA1"><i>The Roots of Pagan Anti-Semitism in the Ancient World</i></a>. Brill Archive. pp.&#160;1–2. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-90-04-04193-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-90-04-04193-6"><bdi>978-90-04-04193-6</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 October</span> 2018</span>. <q>It has long been realised that there are objections to the term anti-Semitism and therefore an endeavour has been made to find a word which better interprets the meaning intended. Already in 1936 Bolkestein, for example, wrote an article on <i>Het "antisemietisme" in de oudheid</i> (Anti-Semitism in the ancient world) in which the word was placed between quotation marks and a preference was expressed for the term hatred of the Jews… Nowadays the term anti-Judaism is often preferred. It certainly expresses better than anti-Semitism the fact that it concerns the attitude to the Jews and avoids any suggestion of racial distinction, which was not or hardly, a factor of any significance in ancient times. For this reason Leipoldt preferred to speak of anti-Judaism when writing his <i>Antisemitsmus in der alien Welt</i> (l933). Bonsirven also preferred this word to Anti-Semitism, "mot moderne qui implique une théorie des races".</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Roots+of+Pagan+Anti-Semitism+in+the+Ancient+World&amp;rft.pages=1-2&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Archive&amp;rft.date=1975&amp;rft.isbn=978-90-04-04193-6&amp;rft.aulast=Sevenster&amp;rft.aufirst=Jan+Nicolaas&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DyLE3AAAAIAAJ%26pg%3DPA1&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 October</span> 2018</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Pogroms+and+Riots%3A+German+Press+Responses+to+Anti-Jewish+Violence+in+Germany+and+Russia+%281881%E2%80%931882%29&amp;rft.pub=Peter+Lang&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=9783631602140&amp;rft.aulast=Weinberg&amp;rft.aufirst=Sonja&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D0HDeEPouQm0C%26pg%3DPA18&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Muravchik2003-189"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Muravchik2003_189-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Joshua Muravchik Marx's aspiration for "the emancipation of society from Judaism" because "the practical Jewish spirit" of "huckstering" had taken over the Christian nations is not that far from the Nazi program's twenty-four point: "combat[ing] the Jewish-materialist spirit within us and without us" in order "that our nation can […] achieve permanent health." See <cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Joshua_Muravchik" title="Joshua Muravchik">Muravchik, Joshua</a> (2003). <i>Heaven on Earth: The Rise and Fall of Socialism</i>. San Francisco: Encounter Books. p.&#160;164. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-893554-45-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-893554-45-0"><bdi>978-1-893554-45-0</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Heaven+on+Earth%3A+The+Rise+and+Fall+of+Socialism&amp;rft.place=San+Francisco&amp;rft.pages=164&amp;rft.pub=Encounter+Books&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-893554-45-0&amp;rft.aulast=Muravchik&amp;rft.aufirst=Joshua&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntisemitism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-266"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-266">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFSachar1961">Sachar 1961</a>, p.&#160;231,</span>

<li id="cite_note-267"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-267">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLaurens2002">Laurens 2002</a>, pp.&#160;467,469–470;'In terms of his initial formation, Haj Amin was far from being an antisemite. He had learnt French at the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Isra%C3%A9lite_Universelle" title="Alliance Israélite Universelle">Alliance Israélite Universelle</a> institute in Jerusalem and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Ant%C3%A9bi" title="Albert Antébi">Albert Antébi</a> had been one of his mentors. In the interwar period, he had fought Zionism as a political and religious leader. He was then of the opinion that the aim of Zionism was to expel the Arabs of Palestine and take over the <a href="/wiki/Haram_al-Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Haram al-Sharif">Haram al-Sharif</a> in order to build the <a href="/wiki/Third_Temple" title="Third Temple">Third Temple</a>. Gradually (<i>progressivement</i>) he was persuaded that world Judaism supported Zionists in an secretive manner and exercised a major influence over decision-making in Great Britain and the United States. For some time (during WW2) he was certain (based on real facts) that the Zionists were seeking to assassinate him. … It is evident that he gradually came to identify his battle in Palestine with that of Germany against world Judaism. The reading of all those passages in his memoirs devoted to his European sojourn reveal an assimilation of the content of european antisemitism, with their two great themes of the identification of Judaism with financial capitalism (Anglo-Saxons), and of the <a href="/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth" title="Stab-in-the-back myth">legend of the stab in the back</a> (the Jews as responsible for the two world wars). On the other hand, a racist vision of world history is totally absent from his general worldview. … Taken together, his writings after 1945 do not show him as having an attitude of <a href="/wiki/Negationism" class="mw-redirect" title="Negationism">holocaust denial</a>, whilst Arab politicians of the first rank, in the period of Eichmann's trial, had begun to adopt (precisely) this kind of discourse.'</span>
</li>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20050904114449/http://www.coe.int/T/E/human_rights/Ecri/1-ECRI/2-Country-by-country_approach/">Council of Europe, ECRI Country-by-Country Reports</a></li>
